ANNEX 5
ZAIRE
FIRST TRANSPORT REHABILITATION PROJECT (ONATRAISNCZ)
Detailed Economic Analysis
Matadi Port
1.       At Matadi Port, the project ibplementation will result in
significant improvement in operational efficiency. Except in 1987, the
port traffic has grown continuously since 1979. According to traffic
forecast (middle assumption), the maximum capacity (2.5 milliun ton) of the
port will be exceeded in 1993. Average general cargo ship waiting '.ime
would then be about 3 days. For general cargo quays, the occupancy rate is
estimated to reach 85X in 1990 and 94% in 1995, while container berths
would remain largely sufficient (occupancy rate of 33.5% in 2000).
Capacity extensions will therefore be necessary in the 1990-1995 period.
2.       The rehabilitation of quays 3 and 4 is necessary to meet the
future capacity gap. A reallocation of space in front of these quays will
allow the extension of yards and the circulation of light vehicles instead
of trains. This change will yield significant gains in handling
operations, especially for logs. As a consequence, ship immobilization
will decrease due to increased operation efficiency: loading performances
will be 550 tons a day for logs and 330 tons a day for fresh food, instead
of 470 and 300 tons a day respectively. As the average value of ship-
waiting time has been taken at $6,000 for regular ships, $15,000 for
container ships and $4,500 for bulk ships, this improvement will generate
large savings in ship-waiting time, which represent about 90% of the
benefits of the quay component. Another ga4n is to avoid major maintenance
expenses that will definitely be necessary in the short term if the quays
are not rehabilitated.
3.       The rehabilitation of 14 quayside cranes will also improve the
port capacity. Without the project, the availability of these cranes is
assumed to decline to 60% in 1990, 45% in 1995 and 30% in 2000. This
situation would oblige port operators to substitute quayside crane handling
by ship gear handling, with a lower efficiency (-20%) and a higher ship
immobilization rate. Another benefit from this component are savings in
maintenance expenses that would be necessary to ensure a lower
availability assumed in the reference scenario.
4.       Two other components also play a role in the port performance
improvement: (i) the new cargo handling equipment (forklifts, log handling
dozers, tractors, mobile cranes, etc.) is assumed to increase operating
efficiency by 3%, which is a very conservative assumption (a consultant
estimate in another study is 7%); (2) the new maintenance shop will
generate an overall improvement of equipment availability in the port,
leading to a 2% reduction in ship immobilization. The profitability of the
various Matadi Port components is shown below:

CFMK Railway
5.       The principal benefits of the CFMK components derive from increased
operating speeds and better equipment availability which can be translated
into a larger operating capacity. Any gain in capacity will reduce the need
in equipment that would otherwise have to be purchased by the compaly. At
the same time, speed increase will generate savings in immobilization of
equipment and freight. In 1986, 51 interruptions occured on the main track
and the equivalent of 378 hours, or 16 days, was therefore lost for
operations. Every wasted day costs about $14,000 in loco, wagon and freight
immobilization. The indirect effects, in terms of scheduling difficulties,
low reliability of shipments, and damage to ONATRA image, were even worse.
6.       Track maintenance equipment is a profitable investment, due to the
combined savings allowed by an efficient inspectiorL and repair system (track
recording car, mobilt cranes, intervention vehicles):
i)    speed increase of the trains: the better condition of a
controlled track and the reduction of repair delay will
lessen the derailments or their consequences. As a result,
an average gain of half an hour will be obtained on the
Matadi-Kinshasa freight trip (i.e. 3% of the total travel
time without stops, which currently lasts 15.74 hours,;
(ii)   lower cost of maintenance t-orks: the replacement of a line
loco by a versatile mobile tracto-crane will result in fuel,
personnel and depreciation savings.
7.       The modernization of 350 wagons will result in significant benefits
in operating efficiency (40% decrease in failures provoked by hot oil boxes)
and iii maintenance costs (less periodic maintenance operations). The civil
works at Limete and Mbanza-Ngungu workshops will increase maintenance
efficiency in these facilities (new berths, additional crane structure) and
improve the locomotive availability by about 4%. The purchase of spare parts
for locos and wagons will also result in an increased availability of the
fleet and lessen the convoy immobilizatioxis by an estimated rate of 10%. The
profitability of the various CFMK railway components is shown below:

Kinshasa Port
8.       The light investment planned in Kinshasa Port is aimed at improving
equipment availability and efficiency, to reduce ship and freight
immobilization. The new maintenance shop is estimated to allow a gain of 15%
in availability rate of cranes and forklifts and extend for 3 years the
economic life of this equipment, reducing substantially the depreciation
costs. It will also result in a 3% decrease of immobilization costs. The
new handling equipment will essentially diminish the waiting and
immobilization time of convoys, since the loading/unloading operations will
be faster (20% gain on general cargo and bagged goods, 14% gain on copper and
other goods). The rehabilitation of quayside cranes will avoid frequent
failures of this equipment and reduce handling delay by 20% in 1990 and 25%
in 1995. The profitability of the various Kinshasa Port components is shown
below:

River Trarsport and Shipyards
9.       River transport and shipyards also need small investment to raise
the cost-effectiveness of their activities whith is low. However, a minimum
investment is absolutely necessary in both entities to maintain the priority
of operations on the Voie Nationale and avoid any disruption in service while
the privatization process of some of the less profitable activities is
completed.  The main benefits of ONATRA's fleet renewal are:
(i)    maintenance savings on new barges and pushers;
(ii)   fuel savings allowed by an optimization of pusher motors;
(iii)  a new convoy operation syatem, where barges wait for the
pusher (and not the contrary), which increases the convoy
turnover, but requires the purchase of a buffer stock of
barges.
10.      As shown in the teble below, the profitability of passenger barges
is low. This is due to difficulties of quantifying the real benefits to
passenger services, which role is important in the Zairean economy, as
considerable freight is carried by most passengers. The food and general
goods supply of Kinshasa and the Zaire basin largely depends on the
availability of river transport. The benefits for local agriculture, trade,
social and cultural exchanges are important, but the lack af statistics
prevents the quantification of these benefits.

SNCZ Railway
11.      SNCZ's major investment is a large track renewal component (about
$70 million in civil works, rail, sleepers and quarry machinery) which
represents 46% of the project total amount. This renewal will improve SNCZ's
operations in the Central and Southern Regions, in particular:
(i)    the decrease in derailments and track failures will diminish
the traffic interruptions (and therefore the convoy
immobilization costs) and the repair costs. 52 derailments
and 123 rail fractures occured in 1986 on the sections to be
renewed. Each derailment results in a repair cost estimated
at $40,800. Considering the impact on the SNCZ network, an
average traffic interruption of 22 hours per derailment
causes a total immobilization time of about 230 train hours;
(ii)   the track improvement (either in renewed sections or in the
sections where released materials will be reutilized) will
allow a direct speed increase (approximately 8%), and
therefore decrease in train immobilization (equipment,
personnel, freight, passengers);
(iii)  the better equipment as;ailability will therefore contribute
to addressing the issue of the limited traction capacity in
SNCZ;
(iv)   the track improvement will also allow considerable gains in
reliability, so that the company will be able to establish an
efficient train scheduling ("plan de transport") on the
network;
(v)    finally, the 303 km track renewal will reduce heavy
maintenance costs that would be necessary to avoid further
damages to the infrastructure assumed in the reference
scenario.
The maintenance costs without renewal would be approximatively 9 times as
expensiie as the maintenance costs of renewed track ($1.220 million per year,
vs. $0.137 million per year).
12.      The locomotive and telecommunications components also address the
issue of rationalizing and mndernizing train operations on the SNCZ system.
The replacement of both line and shunting locos will result in (i) savings on
the expensive rehabilitation of the overaging fleet; (ii) maintenance and
spare parts savings; (iii) operational savings in fuel and personnel and (iv)
rental savings on foreign locos. The telecommunications component will allow

turnover and a quicker attention to accident emergencies. The profitability

ANNEX 6
ZAIRE
FIRST TRANSPORT REHABILITATION PROJECT (ONATRAISNCZ)
Assumptions underlying the Financial Projections
General Note
The financial projections are based on presently available
estimates of exchange rates and inflation; however, these parameters are
volatile and the sensitivity of ONATRA's and SNCZ's finances to them
strongly affects the reliability of the projections. No account has been
taken of economies that will result from ONATRA's reorganization because it
is still in its early stages, and sufficiently reliable data to be
incorporated in the projections is not yet available.
Detailed assumptions are shown in Tables 7.04 (ONATRA) and 7.08
(SNCZ). Basic assumptions for both enterprises are as follows:
(i)   All amounts are in current values.  Exchange rates are those
used in connection with the SAL program.
(ii) Costs of supplies and services are expected to increase in
line with forecast increases in the Zaire CPI, which itself closely follows
the exchange rate and allows for international inflation. Costs in
previous years have not varied significantly with fluctuations in traffic;
this tendancy is expected to continue, and costs have not been assumed to
increase with traffic. This assumption also allows for improved financial
awareness and cost controls.
(iii) Traffic projections are those used in the economic analysis.
(iv) Fixed assets and long-term debt have been revalued in
accordance with the forecast zaire/SDR exchange rate at the end of each
year; no prc-iision has been made for short-term exchange losses or gains as
in the past net gains have been recorded and in accordance with accepted
accounting convention no credit is taken for gains in statements until they
are actually realized.
(v) Debt service: Loan interest has been calculated at an
average rate of 7.5Z on outstanding debt throughout the period of the
projecitons. Repayments of principal have been assumed to average one-
twentieth of outstanding debt.
Basic assumptions for each enterprise are:
I. ONATRA
(i)    Staff is expected to reduce, initially as a result of measures
already taken and early retirements financed as part of the proposed



- 116 -
project, and subsequently through natural wastage and redeployment, by
averages declining from 3.5% in 1988 to 1.9% in 1985. Salaries are
expected to closely follow inflation.
(ii)   Tariffst  ONATRA's proposed increases of 50% and 30% for 1988
and 50% for 1989; thereafter tariffs are raised annually in line with
projected inflation.
(iii) Depreciation has been calculated at an average annual rate of
3.5% on gross revalued fixed assets; this is it. line with ONATRA's average
depreciation rates in past years.
II. SNCZ
(i)    Staff:  as a result of the rerorms introduced by SNCZ's new
management and the early retirements financed as part of the proposed
project, numbers employed are expected to fall from their current level of
21,800 to 18,500 by end-1992 and 18,000 by end-1995.
(ii) Tariff increases have been calculated in line with SNCZ's
proposals for 1988 and thereafter to match cost increases.
